‚óè Plan(Analyze chat loop and UI issues)

‚óè User approved Claude's plan
  ‚éø ¬†Plano de Corre√ß√£o: Chat Loop e Layout 3 Colunas

     Problemas Identificados

     1. Chat em loop infinito: Mensagens duplicadas - WebSocket adiciona mensagens E banco recarrega tudo
     2. Progresso travado em 0%: Progress como mensagem de chat ao inv√©s de componente separado
     3. Documento vazio: N√£o carrega conte√∫do real da API ap√≥s conclus√£o
     4. Layout 2 colunas: Faltando terceira coluna para DocumentActionsCard
     5. Barra de progresso dentro do chat: Deveria estar fora

     Solu√ß√£o

     1. Remover duplica√ß√£o de mensagens (DocumentsPage.tsx)

     - Remover todas as chamadas addChatMessage() do handler WebSocket
     - Usar APENAS recarregamento peri√≥dico do banco via loadChatHistory()
     - WebSocket serve s√≥ para saber quando recarregar

     2. Extrair barra de progresso

     - Criar estado separado: progressPercentage e currentTask
     - Atualizar do WebSocket tipo progress
     - Renderizar <ProgressBar> fora do chat, acima dele

     3. Carregar documento real na conclus√£o

     - Quando execution_completed, chamar getRequirementsDocument(sessionId)
     - Salvar em estado: generatedDocument
     - Passar para DocumentActionsCard na 3¬™ coluna

     4. Layout 3 colunas (DocumentsPage.css + tsx)

     [Sidebar 350px] [Chat flex:1] [Actions Card 400px]
     - CSS: grid-template-columns: 350px 1fr 400px
     - Adicionar <div className="actions-panel"> com DocumentActionsCard
     - Card s√≥ aparece quando documento existe

     5. Fechar WebSocket corretamente

     - Garantir ws.close() ap√≥s execution_completed ou execution_failed
     - Limpar interval de reload

     Arquivos a Modificar

     1. DocumentsPage.tsx (~150 linhas mudadas)
       - Handler WebSocket simplificado
       - Estado de progresso separado
       - Layout 3 colunas
       - Carregar documento da API
     2. DocumentsPage.css (~20 linhas)
       - Grid 3 colunas
       - Estilos para ProgressBar e actions-panel
     3. Criar ProgressBar.tsx (novo componente ~50 linhas)
       - Componente visual de progresso
       - Props: percentage, currentTask

     Resultado Esperado

     ‚úÖ Chat para de rolar infinitamente
     ‚úÖ Progresso vis√≠vel fora do chat
     ‚úÖ Documento aparece completo no card da 3¬™ coluna
     ‚úÖ Layout organizado em 3 colunas
     ‚úÖ WebSocket fecha ao terminar

  Desculpa, voc√™ estava certo - eu n√£o estava prestando aten√ß√£o no detalhe crucial do log.

  O Problema Real:

  O CrewAI retorna a resposta do agente aninhada assim:
  {
      "team_result": "```json\n{...toda a resposta do agente...}\n```"
  }

  O documento markdown ESTAVA L√Å (vis√≠vel no seu log anterior), mas o c√≥digo estava procurando requirements_document_md no n√≠vel errado do JSON.

  A Corre√ß√£o:

  Agora a fun√ß√£o validate_requirements_output_func():

  2. ‚úÖ Extrai a string de dentro dela
  3. ‚úÖ Remove os backticks markdown ( ```json e ```)

‚îÇ  upload\n```\n\n**Passos:**\n1. **Passo 1:** O usu√°rio seleciona o arquivo.\n   - Ator: ACTOR-001\n    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  - A√ß√£o: Seleciona o arquivo a ser enviado.\n   - Sistema: Responde com a verifica√ß√£o do               ‚îÇ

‚îÇ  Exce√ß√£o:**\n- **Exc-1:** O sistema trata erros de upload.\n\n**Estados Finais:**\n- Sucesso: Upload   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  bem-sucedido.\n- Falha: Upload falhou.\n\n**Requisitos Relacionados:** FR-001, BR-002\n\n---\n\n##    ‚îÇ

‚óè User approved Claude's plan
  ‚éø ¬†Plano de Corre√ß√£o: Garantir Carregamento do Documento Gerado

     Problema Identificado

     O documento de requisitos est√° sendo gerado e salvo corretamente no banco (17KB confirmado nos logs), mas o frontend n√£o est√° exibindo porque loadGeneratedDocument() s√≥ √© 
     chamada uma vez quando o WebSocket emite execution_completed, e algo est√° falhando nesse momento.

     Solu√ß√£o: M√∫ltiplas Camadas de Garantia

     1. Adicionar Polling de Fallback (DocumentsPage.tsx)

     Objetivo: Verificar periodicamente se o documento est√° pronto durante o processamento

     Mudan√ßa:
     - Adicionar useEffect que roda a cada 10s enquanto isChatProcessing=true
     - Chama loadGeneratedDocument() periodicamente
     - Para automaticamente quando an√°lise termina

     2. Refor√ßar Evento WebSocket (DocumentsPage.tsx)

     Objetivo: Tentar m√∫ltiplas vezes quando receber execution_completed

     Mudan√ßa:
     - Chamar loadGeneratedDocument() imediatamente
     - Adicionar retry com setTimeout ap√≥s 2 segundos
     - Logs para debug

     3. Melhorar Logs de Debug (DocumentsPage.tsx + requirementsService.ts)

     Objetivo: Identificar exatamente onde/quando est√° falhando

     Mudan√ßa:
     - Logs em loadGeneratedDocument() mostrando cada etapa
     - Logs na API getRequirementsDocument() mostrando request/response
     - Console warnings se documento vier vazio

     4. Verificar Coluna no Banco (OPCIONAL - apenas se necess√°rio)

     Objetivo: Garantir que a coluna existe no banco de dados

     Mudan√ßa:
     - Se a coluna requirements_document n√£o existir, criar via ALTER TABLE
     - Migration SQL: ALTER TABLE execution_sessions ADD COLUMN requirements_document LONGTEXT

     Arquivos a Modificar

     1. src/pages/DocumentsPage.tsx (~1100 linhas)
       - Adicionar polling useEffect
       - Adicionar retry no WebSocket handler
       - Adicionar logs detalhados
     2. src/services/requirementsService.ts (~59 linhas)
       - Adicionar logs na chamada da API
       - Melhorar tratamento de erros
     3. (Opcional) database/migrations/004_add_requirements_document.sql (novo arquivo)
       - Criar coluna se n√£o existir

     Impacto

     - ‚úÖ N√£o quebra funcionalidade existente (apenas adiciona redund√¢ncia)
     - ‚úÖ Performance m√≠nima (polling s√≥ durante an√°lise, ~1 req/10s)
     - ‚úÖ Debug facilitado (logs mostram exatamente onde falha)
     - ‚úÖ Garantia de carregamento (m√∫ltiplas tentativas)

     Resultado Esperado

     Documento ser√° carregado e exibido corretamente na 3¬™ coluna (DocumentActionsCard) sempre que a an√°lise terminar, independente de problemas com WebSocket timing.

  ‚éø ¬†[master be2a0cf] Fix: Garantir carregamento do documento gerado com m√∫ltiplas camadas

‚óè ‚úÖ CORRE√á√ïES IMPLEMENTADAS COM SUCESSO!

  üìä Resumo das Mudan√ßas

  Implementei 4 camadas de garantia para que o documento de requisitos seja sempre carregado e exibido:

  ---
  1. POLLING DE FALLBACK üîÑ

  Arquivo: src/pages/DocumentsPage.tsx:69-84

  // Tenta carregar documento a cada 10 segundos durante an√°lise
  useEffect(() => {
    if (!isChatProcessing || !currentSessionId) return;

    const intervalId = setInterval(() => {
      console.log('üîÑ Polling: Tentando carregar documento...');
      loadGeneratedDocument(currentSessionId);
    }, 10000);

    return () => clearInterval(intervalId);
  }, [isChatProcessing, currentSessionId]);

  Benef√≠cio: Carrega documento mesmo se o WebSocket falhar ou atrasar.

  ---
  2. RETRY NO WEBSOCKET ‚ö°

  Arquivo: src/pages/DocumentsPage.tsx:389-418

  // Tentativas m√∫ltiplas ao receber execution_completed
  loadGeneratedDocument(sessionId);           // Imediato

  setTimeout(() => {
    loadGeneratedDocument(sessionId);         // Ap√≥s 2s
  }, 2000);

  setTimeout(() => {
    loadGeneratedDocument(sessionId);         // Ap√≥s 5s
  }, 5000);

  Benef√≠cio: Garante que lat√™ncia ou timing n√£o impe√ßam carregamento.

  ---

‚óè Explore(Analisar regress√µes do √∫ltimo commit)
  ‚éø ¬†Done (22 tool uses ¬∑ 41.7k tokens ¬∑ 2m 9s)                                                                                                                                    

‚óè üîç AN√ÅLISE COMPLETA - CAUSA RAIZ DOS PROBLEMAS

  Baseado na investiga√ß√£o profunda, identifiquei exatamente o que est√° quebrado:

  ---
  ‚ùå PROBLEMA #1: Race Condition no Polling

  O que acontece:
  1. An√°lise termina ‚Üí WebSocket envia execution_completed
  2. C√≥digo seta setIsChatProcessing(false) IMEDIATAMENTE (linha 444)
  3. Isso DESLIGA o polling (que s√≥ roda se isChatProcessing === true)
  4. As 3 tentativas de carregar documento (imediato, +2s, +5s) executam
  5. MAS o backend pode ainda n√£o ter commitado no banco
  6. Todas as 3 tentativas retornam vazio
  7. Polling est√° desligado, ent√£o nunca mais tenta
  8. RESULTADO: generatedDocument fica vazio permanentemente

  ---
  ‚ùå PROBLEMA #2: Modal N√£o Sincroniza Estado

  MarkdownEditorModal.tsx linha 20:
  const [editedContent, setEditedContent] = useState(content);

  Problema: O estado interno √© inicializado UMA VEZ na montagem. Quando a prop content muda depois, o estado interno N√ÉO atualiza.

  Resultado: Mesmo que o documento seja carregado depois, o editor mostra vazio.

  ---
  ‚ùå PROBLEMA #3: Backend Pode Estar Salvando String Vazia

  Se requirements_document_md n√£o est√° no result_state (por causa do bug de extra√ß√£o do JSON aninhado), o documento √© salvo como "" (string vazia).

  ---
  üìã PLANO DE CORRE√á√ÉO
  ‚éø ¬†User rejected Claude's plan:
     ‚ï≠‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ïÆ
     ‚îÇ Plano: Corrigir Race Condition e Estado N√£o Sincronizado                                             ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                      ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ Problemas Identificados                                                                              ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                      ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ 1. Race Condition: Polling √© desativado ANTES do documento ser salvo no banco                        ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ 2. Modal n√£o sincroniza: Estado interno do editor n√£o atualiza quando prop content muda              ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ 3. Backend pode salvar vazio: Se extra√ß√£o do JSON aninhado falhar, salva ""                          ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                      ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ Causa Raiz                                                                                           ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                      ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ Quando execution_completed acontece:                                                                 ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ - setIsChatProcessing(false) √© chamado imediatamente (linha 444)                                     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ - Isso DESLIGA o polling (linha 76: if (!isChatProcessing || !currentSessionId) return;)             ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ - As 3 tentativas (imediato, +2s, +5s) executam MAS banco pode n√£o ter commitado                     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ - Todas retornam vazio                                                                               ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ - Polling est√° desligado ‚Üí nunca mais tenta                                                          ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ - generatedDocument fica vazio permanentemente                                                       ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                      ‚îÇ

‚óè Perfeito! Agora vou te explicar o que foi corrigido:

  Resposta direta √† sua pergunta:

  O documento NUNCA parou de ser gravado no banco. O c√≥digo do backend (documents.py) n√£o foi alterado no commit 82c89b5 - s√≥ o frontend foi modificado.

  O problema real era:

  RACE CONDITION no frontend - O polling parava ANTES do documento carregar:

  1. An√°lise completa ‚Üí execution_completed dispara
  2. setIsChatProcessing(false) era chamado IMEDIATAMENTE (linha 444)
  3. Isso DESLIGAVA O POLLING (que s√≥ roda se isChatProcessing === true)
  4. As 3 tentativas de retry rodavam mas eram muito cedo (backend ainda commitando)
  5. Polling j√° estava parado, ent√£o nunca tentava de novo
  6. Resultado: generatedDocument ficava vazio permanentemente

  Corre√ß√µes aplicadas:

  Backend (documents.py):

  - ‚úÖ Logging detalhado ANTES do save
  - ‚úÖ Captura affected_rows do UPDATE
  - ‚úÖ Query de verifica√ß√£o p√≥s-save comparando tamanho salvo vs enviado
  - ‚úÖ Logs completos mostram se save foi bem-sucedido

  Frontend (DocumentsPage.tsx):

  - ‚úÖ REMOVIDO setIsChatProcessing(false) do handler execution_completed
  - ‚úÖ Polling continua ativo at√© documento carregar
  - ‚úÖ Timeout de 30s como fallback de seguran√ßa
  - ‚úÖ loadGeneratedDocument() desliga polling SOMENTE ap√≥s sucesso
  - ‚úÖ Combina√ß√£o: polling 10s + 3 retries manuais = m√∫ltiplas tentativas garantidas

  Modais:

  - ‚úÖ MarkdownEditorModal: useEffect sincroniza estado quando content muda
  - ‚úÖ MarkdownViewerModal: Logging para debug

  Agora teste novamente e acompanhe os logs! Voc√™ vai ver:
  1. Backend salvando documento com tamanho confirmado
  2. Frontend tentando m√∫ltiplas vezes at√© carregar
  3. Polling continuando at√© sucesso
  4. Modal abrindo com conte√∫do correto

  H√° um conflito de CSS entre dois componentes usando a mesma classe .viewer-content:

  Causa Raiz

  1. MarkdownViewerModal usa a classe .viewer-content (definida em MarkdownEditorModal.css)
  2. RequirementsDocumentViewer TAMB√âM usa a classe .viewer-content (definida em RequirementsDocumentViewer.css)

  O RequirementsDocumentViewer.css tem:

    display: flex;  /* <-- ISSO EST√Å QUEBRANDO O MODAL */
    flex: 1;
    overflow: hidden;
  }

  Como ambos os CSS s√£o globais, o display: flex do RequirementsDocumentViewer est√° sendo aplicado ao MarkdownViewerModal, causando o layout em colunas horizontais.

  Solu√ß√£o

  Renomear a classe .viewer-content no MarkdownViewerModal para algo √∫nico como .markdown-viewer-content para evitar o conflito.

  2. src/components/documents/MarkdownEditorModal.css - renomear todas as regras .viewer-content para .markdown-viewer-content

        4    # Document Analysis Tasks
        5    analyze_document:
        6      description: >
        7 -      [2.1.1 - Document Types & 2.1.2 - Document Analysis] Analyze document at '{document_path}' (type: {document_type}).
        8 -      Support: PDFs, DOCs, presentations, spreadsheets, TXT, MD, technical artifacts (diagrams, schemas, API docs, code).
        9 -      Extract: (1) Full text content; (2) Document structure (sections, headings, lists, tables); (3) Entities (actors, systems, processes, rules);
       10 -      (4) Implicit/explicit workflows; (5) Domain-specific terminology; (6) Metadata (author, date, version).
       11 -      Identify relationships and dependencies between components.
        7 +      [Document Content Extraction] You will receive one or more documents to analyze.
        8 +      Document information: {document_path} (type: {document_type}).
        9 +  
       10 +      CRITICAL INSTRUCTION: Use the document_reader tool to extract the COMPLETE TEXT from the document(s).
       11 +      DO NOT skip this step. The entire analysis depends on having the full document content.
       12 +  
       13 +      STEP 1 - EXTRACT FULL CONTENT:
       14 +      - Use document_reader tool with the provided document_path and document_type
       15 +      - Extract ALL text content - do not skip any sections
       16 +      - If extraction fails or returns empty/minimal content, RETURN AN ERROR immediately
       17 +      - Verify you extracted at least 100 words (for real documents)
       18 +  
       19 +      STEP 2 - ANALYZE STRUCTURE:
       20 +      From the ACTUAL EXTRACTED TEXT, identify and extract:
       21 +      (1) Document structure: Sections, headings, subheadings, hierarchical organization
       22 +      (2) Entities mentioned: Actors, systems, processes, business concepts, data objects
       23 +      (3) Workflows described: Step-by-step processes, procedures, sequences
       24 +      (4) Domain terminology: Technical terms, jargon, acronyms, specialized vocabulary
       25 +      (5) Relationships: How entities connect, dependencies mentioned
       26 +      (6) Metadata: Author, date, version if present in the document
       27 +  
       28 +      STEP 3 - VALIDATE EXTRACTION:
       29 +      - Count words extracted (must be > 100 for real documents)
       30 +      - Report extraction status: success or failed
       31 +      - Log any issues encountered
       32 +  
       33 +      IMPORTANT:
       34 +      - DO NOT invent or hallucinate content
       35 +      - EXTRACT verbatim text from the document
       36 +      - PRESERVE original wording and structure
       37 +      - If multiple documents, process ALL of them
       38      expected_output: >
       39 -      JSON object: (1) 'content': full text; (2) 'structure': hierarchical structure; (3) 'entities': extracted actors, systems, processes;
       40 -      (4) 'workflows': detected workflows with steps; (5) 'terminology': domain terms with definitions; (6) 'relationships': detected dependencies;
       41 -      (7) 'metadata': file info, stats (word/page count), parsing timestamp.
       39 +      JSON object with:
       40 +      (1) 'content': Complete extracted text from ALL documents (verbatim)

       42 +      (3) 'entities': List of actors/systems/processes/concepts mentioned in the text
       43 +      (4) 'workflows': Process flows/procedures described in the documents

       45 +      (6) 'relationships': Dependencies/connections mentioned in documents
       46 +      (7) 'metadata': Document info, word count (MUST be > 100), extraction timestamp

        48    
        49    extract_requirements:
        50      description: >
        51 -      [2.1.2 - Requirements Analysis] Analyze document content: {document_content}. Additional instructions: {additional_instructions}.
        52 -      Project context: {project_name}, {project_description}.
        53 -      Extract and categorize: (1) Functional Requirements (FR-XXX): unique IDs, clear descriptions, priority (high/medium/low), affected actors, source section, 
           - dependencies;
        54 -      (2) Non-Functional Requirements (NFR-XXX): ID, description, category (performance/security/usability/reliability/scalability/maintainability), measurable 
           - metrics, priority, acceptance criteria;
        55 -      (3) Business Rules (BR-XXX): ID, description, condition, action, affected entities, rationale;
        56 -      (4) Actors/Stakeholders: name, role, responsibilities, interaction points;
        57 -      (5) Entities & Relationships: entity name, attributes, relationships (1-1, 1-N, N-N), cardinality, constraints;
        58 -      (6) Workflows: workflow ID, name, trigger, steps, decision points, end states;
        59 -      (7) Domain Glossary: term, definition, context, synonyms, related terms.
        60 -      Detect implicit requirements and dependencies between requirements.
        51 +      [Requirements Extraction from Document Content] Extract system requirements from analyzed documents.
        52 +  
        53 +      YOU WILL RECEIVE:
        54 +      - document_content: {document_content} (FULL TEXT from documents - may be multiple documents concatenated)
        55 +      - Additional context: {additional_instructions}
        56 +      - Project: {project_name} - {project_description}
        57 +  
        58 +      CRITICAL VALIDATION:
        59 +      STEP 0 - VERIFY INPUT:
        60 +      - Check if document_content field contains actual text (NOT empty, NOT just a path/URL)
        61 +      - If document_content is empty or less than 100 words, STOP and return ERROR status
        62 +      - The document_content should contain the COMPLETE extracted text from all uploaded documents
        63 +  
        64 +      STEP 1 - READ AND UNDERSTAND:
        65 +      - Read the ENTIRE document_content carefully
        66 +      - Identify the domain/subject area from the content (healthcare, finance, logistics, government, etc.)
        67 +      - Understand the context and purpose described in the documents
        68 +      - Note any specific regulations, standards, or frameworks mentioned
        69 +  
        70 +      STEP 2 - EXTRACT REQUIREMENTS FROM TEXT:
        71 +      Analyze the document content line-by-line and extract requirements ONLY from what is:
        72 +      - Explicitly stated in the text
        73 +      - Strongly implied by the context
        74 +      - Required by regulations/standards mentioned in the documents
        75 +  
        76 +      DO NOT invent generic requirements. Every requirement MUST be traceable to the document content.
        77 +  
        78 +      For EACH requirement you extract, you MUST provide:
        79 +      - Source: Which document (if multiple) and which section/paragraph
        80 +      - Quote: Verbatim text from the document that led to this requirement
        81 +      - Interpretation: Your translation of that text into a clear requirement statement
        82 +  
        83 +      STEP 3 - CATEGORIZE AND STRUCTURE:
        84 +      Extract the following categories from the ACTUAL DOCUMENT TEXT:
        85 +  
        86 +      (1) FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENTS (FR-XXX):
        87 +         - ID: Sequential (FR-001, FR-002, ...)
        88 +         - Description: What the system must DO (actions, features, capabilities)
        89 +         - Priority: High/Medium/Low (infer from language: "must"=high, "should"=medium, "could"=low)
        90 +         - Actors: Who uses/interacts with this functionality
        91 +         - Source: Document name + section/page where found
        92 +         - Source quote: Exact text from document
        93 +         - Dependencies: Other requirements this depends on
        94 +         - Acceptance criteria: How to verify this requirement is met
        95 +  
        96 +      (2) NON-FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENTS (NFR-XXX):
        97 +         - ID: Sequential (NFR-001, NFR-002, ...)
        98 +         - Description: Quality attributes (performance, security, usability, etc.)
        99 +         - Category: Performance/Security/Usability/Reliability/Scalability/Maintainability
       100 +         - Measurable metric: Specific measurement (e.g., "< 2 seconds", "99.9% uptime", "AES-256 encryption")
       101 +         - Priority: High/Medium/Low
       102 +         - Source: Document name + section where found
       103 +         - Source quote: Exact text from document
       104 +  
       105 +      (3) BUSINESS RULES (BR-XXX):
       106 +         - ID: Sequential (BR-001, BR-002, ...)
       107 +         - Description: Business constraints and policies
       108 +         - Condition: When/If clause (trigger)
       109 +         - Action: Then clause (what happens)
       110 +         - Affected entities: What data/objects are impacted
       111 +         - Rationale: WHY this rule exists (from document context)
       112 +         - Source: Document name + section where found
       113 +  
       114 +      (4) ACTORS/STAKEHOLDERS:
       115 +         - Name: Specific role names from documents (e.g., "Patient", "Admin", "Auditor")
       116 +         - Role: What they do
       117 +         - Responsibilities: Their duties as described
       118 +         - Interaction points: Where they interact with the system
       119 +         - Source: Where mentioned in documents
       120 +  
       121 +      (5) ENTITIES & DATA OBJECTS:
       122 +         - Entity name: Key data concepts from documents
       123 +         - Attributes: Properties mentioned
       124 +         - Relationships: How entities relate (1-to-1, 1-to-many, many-to-many)
       125 +         - Constraints: Rules governing the entity
       126 +         - Source: Where described in documents
       127 +  
       128 +      (6) WORKFLOWS/PROCESSES:
       129 +         - Workflow ID: Sequential (WF-001, WF-002, ...)
       130 +         - Name: Process name from documents
       131 +         - Trigger: What starts this workflow
       132 +         - Steps: Sequence of actions as described in documents
       133 +         - Decision points: Conditional branches
       134 +         - End states: Possible outcomes
       135 +         - Source: Where described in documents
       136 +  
       137 +      (7) DOMAIN GLOSSARY:
       138 +         - Term: Technical term or acronym used in documents
       139 +         - Definition: As defined in documents (or inferred from context)
       140 +         - Context: How it's used
       141 +         - Synonyms: Alternative terms found
       142 +         - Source: Where first mentioned
       143 +  
       144 +      STEP 4 - INFER IMPLICIT REQUIREMENTS (Carefully):
       145 +      Based on the domain identified and explicit content, you MAY infer requirements that are:
       146 +      - Industry standard for this domain (e.g., if healthcare mentioned ‚Üí likely needs HIPAA compliance)
       147 +      - Technical necessities (e.g., if user accounts mentioned ‚Üí likely needs password reset)
       148 +      - Legal requirements (e.g., if personal data ‚Üí likely needs GDPR/LGPD compliance)
       149 +  
       150 +      Mark ALL implicit requirements clearly as "Implicit - requires confirmation" with justification.
       151 +  
       152 +      STEP 5 - MAP DEPENDENCIES:
       153 +      Create dependency graph showing which requirements depend on others.
       154 +  
       155 +      QUALITY REQUIREMENTS:
       156 +      - Minimum 5 functional requirements (unless document is very small)
       157 +      - EVERY requirement must have source citation
       158 +      - NO generic requirements without specific context from documents
       159 +      - ALL technical terms in glossary
       160 +  
       161      expected_output: >
       162 -      JSON object: 'functional_requirements' (array), 'non_functional_requirements' (array), 'business_rules' (array), 'actors' (array),
       163 -      'entities' (array with attributes and relationships), 'workflows' (array with steps and decision points),
       164 -      'glossary' (array of domain terms), 'requirement_dependencies' (graph of dependencies), 'implicit_requirements' (detected implicit needs).
       162 +      JSON object with complete extraction results:
       163 +      'functional_requirements': array with id, description, priority, actors, source_document, source_section, source_quote, dependencies, acceptance_criteria
       164 +      'non_functional_requirements': array with id, description, category, metric, priority, source_document, source_quote
       165 +      'business_rules': array with id, description, condition, action, entities, rationale, source_document
       166 +      'actors': array with name, role, responsibilities, interaction_points, source_document
       167 +      'entities': array with name, attributes, relationships, constraints, source_document
       168 +      'workflows': array with id, name, trigger, steps, decisions, end_states, source_document
       169 +      'glossary': array with term, definition, context, synonyms, source_document
       170 +      'requirement_dependencies': graph of dependencies between requirements
       171 +      'implicit_requirements': array of inferred requirements with justification and "requires_confirmation: true"
       172 +      'domain_identified': the domain/industry identified from documents
       173 +      'extraction_metadata': word_count_analyzed, sections_processed, confidence_score

       177 -      [2.1.3 - Complementary Verifications] Research complementary info for requirements: {requirements_json}. Additional instructions: {additional_instructions}.
       178 -      Project domain: {project_name}.
       179 -      Perform: (1) Knowledge base queries to enrich domain understanding; (2) Cross-document consistency verification (if multiple docs);

       181 -      (5) Impact-based prioritization (critical path, dependencies, business value).

       183 -      (d) Performance benchmarks; (e) API docs for integrations; (f) Accessibility (WCAG, ADA); (g) Compliance requirements for domain.
       184 -      Prioritize authoritative sources (official docs, standards bodies, .gov, .edu, reputable tech sites).
       177 +      [Web Research and Domain Enrichment] Enrich extracted requirements with industry knowledge and best practices.
       178 +  
       179 +      YOU WILL RECEIVE:
       180 +      - requirements_json: {requirements_json} (extracted requirements from documents)
       181 +      - Project context: {project_name}
       182 +      - Additional instructions: {additional_instructions}
       183 +  
       184 +      STEP 1 - IDENTIFY THE DOMAIN:
       185 +      From the extracted requirements, identify:
       186 +      - Primary industry/domain (e.g., healthcare, finance, e-commerce, logistics, government/public sector, education, manufacturing)
       187 +      - Application type (web application, mobile app, API/backend, desktop, embedded system, data platform)
       188 +      - Key technologies mentioned (databases, frameworks, cloud services, integrations)
       189 +      - Regulations/compliance needs mentioned (GDPR, HIPAA, SOX, PCI-DSS, LGPD, WCAG)
       190 +      - Geographic region if relevant (affects regulations and standards)
       191 +  
       192 +      STEP 2 - FORMULATE DOMAIN-SPECIFIC SEARCH QUERIES:
       193 +      Create TARGETED search queries based on the identified domain and requirements.
       194 +      DO NOT use generic queries - tailor them to the specific domain.
       195 +  
       196 +      EXAMPLES of domain-specific queries:
       197 +      - If domain=healthcare: "HIPAA compliance requirements", "HL7 FHIR standards", "healthcare data security best practices"
       198 +      - If domain=finance: "PCI-DSS requirements", "financial transaction security", "SOX compliance checklist"
       199 +      - If domain=e-commerce: "PCI-DSS e-commerce", "payment gateway integration best practices", "GDPR e-commerce requirements"
       200 +      - If domain=government: "accessibility WCAG 2.1 government", "public sector data protection", "e-government security standards"
       201 +      - If domain=logistics: "supply chain tracking standards", "EDI integration", "warehouse management best practices"
       202 +  
       203 +      Combine domain + functional area + "best practices" or "standards" or "compliance"
       204 +  
       205 +      STEP 3 - WEB RESEARCH CATEGORIES:
       206 +  
       207 +      (a) INDUSTRY BEST PRACTICES:
       208 +          Search for current best practices specific to the identified domain.
       209 +          Query format: "[domain] [functional area] best practices [current year]"
       210 +          Prioritize: Industry publications, whitepapers, case studies from domain leaders
       211 +  
       212 +      (b) TECHNOLOGY STANDARDS/FRAMEWORKS:
       213 +          Find relevant technical standards for technologies mentioned in requirements.
       214 +          Examples: REST API standards, database design patterns, authentication protocols
       215 +          Query format: "[technology] [standard] official documentation"
       216 +  
       217 +      (c) SECURITY & COMPLIANCE:
       218 +          Research applicable security standards based on domain:
       219 +          - ALL domains: OWASP Top 10, secure coding practices
       220 +          - Healthcare: HIPAA, HITECH, HL7, FHIR
       221 +          - Finance: PCI-DSS, SOX, financial data protection
       222 +          - E-commerce: PCI-DSS, consumer data protection
       223 +          - Government: FedRAMP, NIST frameworks, accessibility standards
       224 +          - EU/Brazil: GDPR, LGPD data protection
       225 +          Query format: "[domain] [regulation] compliance requirements"
       226 +  
       227 +      (d) PERFORMANCE BENCHMARKS:
       228 +          Find industry benchmarks for performance metrics:
       229 +          - Response times for similar applications in the domain
       230 +          - Scalability expectations
       231 +          - Availability/uptime requirements (SLA standards)
       232 +          Query format: "[domain] [application type] performance benchmarks"
       233 +  
       234 +      (e) INTEGRATION STANDARDS:
       235 +          If requirements mention integrations, research:
       236 +          - Official API documentation
       237 +          - Integration patterns and examples
       238 +          - Rate limits, quotas, authentication methods
       239 +          Query format: "[system name] API documentation integration"
       240 +  
       241 +      (f) ACCESSIBILITY REQUIREMENTS:
       242 +          Research accessibility standards:
       243 +          - WCAG 2.1 Level AA (minimum for most domains)
       244 +          - ADA compliance (US)
       245 +          - EN 301 549 (European standard)
       246 +          - Domain-specific accessibility needs
       247 +          Query format: "WCAG 2.1 [domain] accessibility requirements"
       248 +  
       249 +      (g) COMPLIANCE CHECKLISTS:
       250 +          Find detailed compliance checklists for the domain:
       251 +          - Regulatory requirements lists
       252 +          - Certification requirements
       253 +          - Audit preparation guides
       254 +          Query format: "[regulation] compliance checklist [domain]"
       255 +  
       256 +      STEP 4 - EVALUATE SOURCE CREDIBILITY:
       257 +      Prioritize sources in this order:
       258 +      1. Official standards bodies (W3C, IETF, ISO, NIST, IEEE)
       259 +      2. Government/regulatory sites (.gov, regulatory agencies)
       260 +      3. Industry associations and consortiums
       261 +      4. Major cloud providers documentation (AWS, Azure, GCP - for cloud/infrastructure)
       262 +      5. Official product documentation (for specific technologies)
       263 +      6. Reputable tech companies engineering blogs (Google, Microsoft, Meta, etc.)
       264 +      7. Academic sources (.edu, research papers)
       265 +      8. Well-known tech publications (only for general guidance)
       266 +  
       267 +      AVOID: Marketing content, outdated sources (>2 years for tech topics), unverified blogs
       268 +  
       269 +      STEP 5 - CROSS-DOCUMENT CONSISTENCY:
       270 +      If multiple documents were analyzed, check for:
       271 +      - Conflicting requirements between documents
       272 +      - Duplicate requirements worded differently
       273 +      - Missing connections between related documents
       274 +      - Versioning issues (outdated information)
       275 +  
       276 +      STEP 6 - DETECT AMBIGUITIES:
       277 +      Identify vague or ambiguous requirements:
       278 +      - Undefined terms or jargon without glossary entry
       279 +      - Quantitative statements without specific values ("fast", "scalable", "secure", "many")
       280 +      - Contradictory statements
       281 +      - Missing critical details (who, what, when, where, how)
       282 +  
       283 +      STEP 7 - GENERATE CLARIFICATION QUESTIONS:
       284 +      For each ambiguity or gap, create SPECIFIC questions for stakeholders:
       285 +      - Not: "How should this work?" (too vague)
       286 +      - But: "Should the system support real-time updates (< 1 sec) or near-real-time (< 30 sec)?"
       287 +      Prioritize by impact: critical path, security, compliance first.
       288 +  
       289 +      STEP 8 - IDENTIFY POTENTIALLY MISSING REQUIREMENTS:
       290 +      Based on research and domain knowledge, identify requirements typically needed but not mentioned:
       291 +      - Standard features for application type (e.g., password reset, session timeout, audit logs)
       292 +      - Legal requirements not mentioned (e.g., cookie consent, terms of service, data retention policies)
       293 +      - Security measures expected for domain (e.g., encryption at rest, MFA, penetration testing)
       294 +      - Operational requirements (backup, monitoring, disaster recovery, performance testing)
       295 +  
       296 +      Mark these as "Potentially Missing - Requires stakeholder confirmation" with justification from research.
       297 +

A empresa informa as caracter√≠sticas t√©cnicas dos produtos por classe, seguindo os crit√©rios normalmente avaliados nos certames.
A IA tamb√©m realiza a leitura dos manuais t√©cnicos e sugere novos campos ou requisitos faltantes para enriquecer o cadastro.

2. Agente de IA para Captura e Leitura dos Certames
Um agente aut√¥nomo monitora diariamente as fontes p√∫blicas (federal, estaduais e municipais) e captura novos editais.
O sistema l√™ o edital, interpreta cl√°usulas t√©cnicas e administrativas e calcula automaticamente o grau de ader√™ncia de cada item aos produtos cadastrados.

3. Sugest√£o de Participa√ß√£o

O agente tamb√©m lista os requisitos t√©cnicos, administrativos e documentais que precisam compor a proposta e os anexos obrigat√≥rios.

A IA monta automaticamente a proposta completa:
        ‚Ä¢       texto t√©cnico aderente ao edital,

STEP 1 - IDENTIFY THE DOMAIN: From the extracted requirements, identify: - Primary industry/domain (e.g., healthcare, finance, e-commerce, logistics, government/public sector, 
education, manufacturing) - Application type (web application, mobile app, API/backend, desktop, embedded system, data platform) - Key technologies mentioned (databases, 
frameworks, cloud services, integrations) - Regulations/compliance needs mentioned (GDPR, HIPAA, SOX, PCI-DSS, LGPD, WCAG) - Geographic region if relevant (affects regulations and 
standards)
STEP 2 - FORMULATE DOMAIN-SPECIFIC SEARCH QUERIES: Create TARGETED search queries based on the identified domain and requirements. DO NOT use generic queries - tailor them to the 
specific domain.
EXAMPLES of domain-specific queries: - If domain=healthcare: "HIPAA compliance requirements", "HL7 FHIR standards", "healthcare data security best practices" - If domain=finance: 
"PCI-DSS requirements", "financial transaction security", "SOX compliance checklist" - If domain=e-commerce: "PCI-DSS e-commerce", "payment gateway integration best practices", 
"GDPR e-commerce requirements" - If domain=government: "accessibility WCAG 2.1 government", "public sector data protection", "e-government security standards" - If 
domain=logistics: "supply chain tracking standards", "EDI integration", "warehouse management best practices"
Combine domain + functional area + "best practices" or "standards" or "compliance"
STEP 3 - WEB RESEARCH CATEGORIES:
(a) INDUSTRY BEST PRACTICES:
    Search for current best practices specific to the identified domain.
    Query format: "[domain] [functional area] best practices [current year]"
    Prioritize: Industry publications, whitepapers, case studies from domain leaders

(b) TECHNOLOGY STANDARDS/FRAMEWORKS:
    Find relevant technical standards for technologies mentioned in requirements.
    Examples: REST API standards, database design patterns, authentication protocols
    Query format: "[technology] [standard] official documentation"

(c) SECURITY & COMPLIANCE:
    Research applicable security standards based on domain:
    - ALL domains: OWASP Top 10, secure coding practices
    - Healthcare: HIPAA, HITECH, HL7, FHIR
    - Finance: PCI-DSS, SOX, financial data protection
    - E-commerce: PCI-DSS, consumer data protection
    - Government: FedRAMP, NIST frameworks, accessibility standards
    - EU/Brazil: GDPR, LGPD data protection
    Query format: "[domain] [regulation] compliance requirements"

(d) PERFORMANCE BENCHMARKS:
    Find industry benchmarks for performance metrics:
    - Response times for similar applications in the domain
    - Scalability expectations
    - Availability/uptime requirements (SLA standards)
    Query format: "[domain] [application type] performance benchmarks"

(e) INTEGRATION STANDARDS:
    If requirements mention integrations, research:
    - Official API documentation
    - Integration patterns and examples
    - Rate limits, quotas, authentication methods
    Query format: "[system name] API documentation integration"

(f) ACCESSIBILITY REQUIREMENTS:
    Research accessibility standards:
    - WCAG 2.1 Level AA (minimum for most domains)
    - ADA compliance (US)
    - EN 301 549 (European standard)
    - Domain-specific accessibility needs
    Query format: "WCAG 2.1 [domain] accessibility requirements"

(g) COMPLIANCE CHECKLISTS:
    Find detailed compliance checklists for the domain:
    - Regulatory requirements lists
    - Certification requirements
    - Audit preparation guides
    Query format: "[regulation] compliance checklist [domain]"

STEP 4 - EVALUATE SOURCE CREDIBILITY: Prioritize sources in this order: 1. Official standards bodies (W3C, IETF, ISO, NIST, IEEE) 2. Government/regulatory sites (.gov, regulatory 
agencies) 3. Industry associations and consortiums 4. Major cloud providers documentation (AWS, Azure, GCP - for cloud/infrastructure) 5. Official product documentation (for 
specific technologies) 6. Reputable tech companies engineering blogs (Google, Microsoft, Meta, etc.) 7. Academic sources (.edu, research papers) 8. Well-known tech publications 
(only for general guidance)
AVOID: Marketing content, outdated sources (>2 years for tech topics), unverified blogs
STEP 5 - CROSS-DOCUMENT CONSISTENCY: If multiple documents were analyzed, check for: - Conflicting requirements between documents - Duplicate requirements worded differently - 
Missing connections between related documents - Versioning issues (outdated information)
STEP 6 - DETECT AMBIGUITIES: Identify vague or ambiguous requirements: - Undefined terms or jargon without glossary entry - Quantitative statements without specific values ("fast",
 "scalable", "secure", "many") - Contradictory statements - Missing critical details (who, what, when, where, how)
STEP 7 - GENERATE CLARIFICATION QUESTIONS: For each ambiguity or gap, create SPECIFIC questions for stakeholders: - Not: "How should this work?" (too vague) - But: "Should the 
system support real-time updates (< 1 sec) or near-real-time (< 30 sec)?" Prioritize by impact: critical path, security, compliance first.
STEP 8 - IDENTIFY POTENTIALLY MISSING REQUIREMENTS: Based on research and domain knowledge, identify requirements typically needed but not mentioned: - Standard features for 
application type (e.g., password reset, session timeout, audit logs) - Legal requirements not mentioned (e.g., cookie consent, terms of service, data retention policies) - Security
 measures expected for domain (e.g., encryption at rest, MFA, penetration testing) - Operational requirements (backup, monitoring, disaster recovery, performance testing)
Mark these as "Potentially Missing - Requires stakeholder confirmation" with justification from research.
, expected_output=JSON object with comprehensive research findings: (1) 'domain_analysis': identified domain, application type, key technologies, compliance needs (2) 
'research_findings': array with source_url, title, summary, relevance_to_requirements, credibility_score (high/medium/low), finding_type 
(best_practice/standard/compliance/technology) (3) 'consistency_issues': array of cross-document conflicts with affected_requirements, conflict_description, severity, 
suggested_resolution (4) 'ambiguities_detected': array with ambiguous_text, location (requirement ID), reason, severity, clarification_question, examples_of_clear_alternatives (5) 
'clarification_questions': array with question, priority (critical/high/medium/low), affected_requirements, context_why_needed, example_valid_answers (6) 'recommended_standards': 
array with name (e.g., "WCAG 2.1 Level AA"), url, description, applicability_reason, implementation_effort (low/medium/high) (7) 'suggested_technologies': array with name, 
use_case, official_docs_url, maturity_score, pros, cons, related_requirements (8) 'compliance_checklist': array with regulation_name, specific_requirement, current_status 
(addressed/partial/missing), related_requirements, gaps_to_fill (9) 'missing_requirements_suggestions': array with proposed_id, description, justification_from_research, priority, 
source_research_finding, requires_confirmation:true (10) 'prioritization_recommendations': impact vs effort analysis (11) 'domain_specific_insights': key insights about the domain 
that affect requirements
)]

‚îÇ  STEP 1 - IDENTIFY THE DOMAIN: From the extracted requirements, identify: - Primary industry/domain    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (e.g., healthcare, finance, e-commerce, logistics, government/public sector, education,               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  manufacturing) - Application type (web application, mobile app, API/backend, desktop, embedded        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  system, data platform) - Key technologies mentioned (databases, frameworks, cloud services,           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  integrations) - Regulations/compliance needs mentioned (GDPR, HIPAA, SOX, PCI-DSS, LGPD, WCAG) -      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Geographic region if relevant (affects regulations and standards)                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  STEP 2 - FORMULATE DOMAIN-SPECIFIC SEARCH QUERIES: Create TARGETED search queries based on the        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  identified domain and requirements. DO NOT use generic queries - tailor them to the specific domain.  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  EXAMPLES of domain-specific queries: - If domain=healthcare: "HIPAA compliance requirements", "HL7    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  FHIR standards", "healthcare data security best practices" - If domain=finance: "PCI-DSS              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  requirements", "financial transaction security", "SOX compliance checklist" - If domain=e-commerce:   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  "PCI-DSS e-commerce", "payment gateway integration best practices", "GDPR e-commerce requirements" -  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  If domain=government: "accessibility WCAG 2.1 government", "public sector data protection",           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  "e-government security standards" - If domain=logistics: "supply chain tracking standards", "EDI      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  integration", "warehouse management best practices"                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Combine domain + functional area + "best practices" or "standards" or "compliance"                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  STEP 3 - WEB RESEARCH CATEGORIES:                                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (a) INDUSTRY BEST PRACTICES:                                                                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Search for current best practices specific to the identified domain.                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Query format: "[domain] [functional area] best practices [current year]"                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Prioritize: Industry publications, whitepapers, case studies from domain leaders                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (b) TECHNOLOGY STANDARDS/FRAMEWORKS:                                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Find relevant technical standards for technologies mentioned in requirements.                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Examples: REST API standards, database design patterns, authentication protocols                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Query format: "[technology] [standard] official documentation"                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (c) SECURITY & COMPLIANCE:                                                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Research applicable security standards based on domain:                                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - ALL domains: OWASP Top 10, secure coding practices                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Healthcare: HIPAA, HITECH, HL7, FHIR                                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Finance: PCI-DSS, SOX, financial data protection                                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - E-commerce: PCI-DSS, consumer data protection                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Government: FedRAMP, NIST frameworks, accessibility standards                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - EU/Brazil: GDPR, LGPD data protection                                                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Query format: "[domain] [regulation] compliance requirements"                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (d) PERFORMANCE BENCHMARKS:                                                                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Find industry benchmarks for performance metrics:                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Response times for similar applications in the domain                                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Scalability expectations                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Availability/uptime requirements (SLA standards)                                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Query format: "[domain] [application type] performance benchmarks"                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (e) INTEGRATION STANDARDS:                                                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      If requirements mention integrations, research:                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Official API documentation                                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Integration patterns and examples                                                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Rate limits, quotas, authentication methods                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Query format: "[system name] API documentation integration"                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (f) ACCESSIBILITY REQUIREMENTS:                                                                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Research accessibility standards:                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - WCAG 2.1 Level AA (minimum for most domains)                                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - ADA compliance (US)                                                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - EN 301 549 (European standard)                                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Domain-specific accessibility needs                                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Query format: "WCAG 2.1 [domain] accessibility requirements"                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (g) COMPLIANCE CHECKLISTS:                                                                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Find detailed compliance checklists for the domain:                                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Regulatory requirements lists                                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Certification requirements                                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      - Audit preparation guides                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      Query format: "[regulation] compliance checklist [domain]"                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  STEP 4 - EVALUATE SOURCE CREDIBILITY: Prioritize sources in this order: 1. Official standards bodies  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  (W3C, IETF, ISO, NIST, IEEE) 2. Government/regulatory sites (.gov, regulatory agencies) 3. Industry   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  associations and consortiums 4. Major cloud providers documentation (AWS, Azure, GCP - for            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  cloud/infrastructure) 5. Official product documentation (for specific technologies) 6. Reputable      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  tech companies engineering blogs (Google, Microsoft, Meta, etc.) 7. Academic sources (.edu, research  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  papers) 8. Well-known tech publications (only for general guidance)                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  AVOID: Marketing content, outdated sources (>2 years for tech topics), unverified blogs               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  STEP 5 - CROSS-DOCUMENT CONSISTENCY: If multiple documents were analyzed, check for: - Conflicting    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  requirements between documents - Duplicate requirements worded differently - Missing connections      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  between related documents - Versioning issues (outdated information)                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  STEP 6 - DETECT AMBIGUITIES: Identify vague or ambiguous requirements: - Undefined terms or jargon    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  without glossary entry - Quantitative statements without specific values ("fast", "scalable",         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  "secure", "many") - Contradictory statements - Missing critical details (who, what, when, where,      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  how)                                                                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  STEP 7 - GENERATE CLARIFICATION QUESTIONS: For each ambiguity or gap, create SPECIFIC questions for   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  stakeholders: - Not: "How should this work?" (too vague) - But: "Should the system support real-time  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  updates (< 1 sec) or near-real-time (< 30 sec)?" Prioritize by impact: critical path, security,       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  compliance first.                                                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  STEP 8 - IDENTIFY POTENTIALLY MISSING REQUIREMENTS: Based on research and domain knowledge, identify  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  requirements typically needed but not mentioned: - Standard features for application type (e.g.,      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  password reset, session timeout, audit logs) - Legal requirements not mentioned (e.g., cookie         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  consent, terms of service, data retention policies) - Security measures expected for domain (e.g.,    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  encryption at rest, MFA, penetration testing) - Operational requirements (backup, monitoring,         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  disaster recovery, performance testing)                                                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Mark these as "Potentially Missing - Requires stakeholder confirmation" with justification from       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  research.                                                                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                                                        ‚îÇ

     ‚îÇ                                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ Nova descri√ß√£o:                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ analyze_document:                                                                                                 ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ   description: >                                                                                                  ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     [Document Content Analysis] You have received PRE-EXTRACTED document content.                                 ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     YOU WILL RECEIVE:                                                                                             ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - document_content: {document_content} (COMPLETE TEXT already extracted from ALL uploaded documents)          ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - document_path: {document_path} (reference only)                                                             ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - additional_instructions: {additional_instructions}                                                          ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     CRITICAL: The document content has ALREADY BEEN EXTRACTED for you.                                            ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     DO NOT try to read files - work with the provided text.                                                       ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     STEP 0 - VALIDATE INPUT:                                                                                      ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Check if document_content is not empty (minimum 100 words)                                                  ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - If empty or too short, STOP and return ERROR                                                                ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     STEP 1 - READ ENTIRE CONTENT:                                                                                 ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Read ALL the document_content provided                                                                      ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Identify what type of content it is (interview, requirements doc, technical spec, etc.)                     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Understand the domain/industry from the content itself                                                      ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     STEP 2 - EXTRACT KEY INFORMATION:                                                                             ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     From the ACTUAL TEXT in document_content, extract:                                                            ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     (1) ACTORS: People, roles, companies mentioned (names, positions, responsibilities)                           ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     (2) BUSINESS CONTEXT: Company description, industry, market, geography                                        ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     (3) PAIN POINTS: Current problems, challenges, bottlenecks explicitly mentioned                               ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     (4) CURRENT PROCESS: How things are done today (tools, workflows, team size)                                  ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     (5) DESIRED SOLUTION: What they want the system to do                                                         ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     (6) DOMAIN CONCEPTS: Technical terms, jargon, business rules, data entities                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     (7) CONSTRAINTS: Regulations, compliance, technical limitations mentioned                                     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     (8) METRICS: Numbers, volumes, performance data mentioned                                                     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     STEP 3 - STRUCTURE ANALYSIS:                                                                                  ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Identify document structure (sections, headings)                                                            ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Map relationships between concepts                                                                          ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Note workflows/processes described                                                                          ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                                                                                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     IMPORTANT:                                                                                                    ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Extract VERBATIM quotes from document_content as evidence                                                   ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - DO NOT invent or assume information not in the text                                                         ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - If multiple documents concatenated, process ALL of them                                                     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ     - Pay special attention to QUANTITATIVE data (numbers, volumes, percentages)                                  ‚îÇ

> pode executar o plano. mas antes me explique por que decidimos usar document_content ao inves de document_reader. o document_content tem o texto dividio em chunks? por isso √© 
mais vantajoso? o document_reader nao suporta documentos longos? 

‚óè √ìtima pergunta! Deixa eu explicar a decis√£o t√©cnica:

  POR QUE USAR document_content AO INV√âS DE document_reader?

  Resposta curta:

  - O document_content J√Å cont√©m o texto COMPLETO extra√≠do de TODOS os documentos
  - N√£o est√° dividido em chunks - √© o texto integral concatenado
  - Usar document_reader seria redundante e desperdi√ßaria tokens do LLM

  An√°lise detalhada:

  1. O que acontece atualmente em documents.py:58-108:

  # LOOP que processa TODOS os documentos
  for doc_id, doc_filename, doc_path in documents:
      parsed = DocumentParser.parse(doc_path)  # ‚Üê Extrai PDF/DOCX aqui
      doc_text = parsed["text"]                 # ‚Üê Texto COMPLETO

      all_documents_content += doc_text         # ‚Üê Concatena TUDO

  # Passa para workflow
  execute_document_analysis_workflow(
      document_content=all_documents_content    # ‚Üê Texto INTEGRAL de TODOS
  )

  Resultado: document_content cont√©m, por exemplo, as 8 p√°ginas completas do PDF da Farmac (milhares de palavras), SEM chunking.

  2. O que o document_reader tool faz (langnettools.py:32-50):

  def _run(self, document_path: str, document_type: str) -> str:
      from app.parsers import DocumentParser
      result = DocumentParser.parse(document_path)  # ‚Üê MESMA extra√ß√£o!
      return result["text"]

  Problema: Faz a MESMA COISA que j√° foi feita no documents.py!

  3. Por que o YAML atual falha:

  O analyze_document task diz (linha 10):
  CRITICAL INSTRUCTION: Use the document_reader tool to extract...

  O que acontece:
  1. Backend extrai PDF ‚Üí 8 p√°ginas de texto em document_content
  2. Agente IGNORA document_content
  3. Agente tenta usar document_reader tool com document_path
  4. Tool tenta extrair PDF de novo (pode falhar se path for "Multiple documents: ...")
  5. DESPERD√çCIO: Extra√ß√£o duplicada + tokens LLM gastos com tool call

  4. Vantagens de usar document_content direto:

  ‚úÖ Efici√™ncia: Extra√ß√£o feita UMA VEZ no backend
  ‚úÖ Confiabilidade: Conte√∫do j√° validado e formatado
  ‚úÖ M√∫ltiplos documentos: J√° concatenados com separadores
  ‚úÖ Menos tokens: N√£o gasta tokens do LLM com tool call
  ‚úÖ Mais contexto: LLM recebe texto direto na descri√ß√£o da task

  5. O document_reader suporta documentos longos?
